RATING: 8
Sentinels of the Multiverse is a cooperative, fixed-deck card game with a comic book flavor. Each player plays as one of ten heroes, against one of four villains, and the battle takes place in one of four different dynamic environments. Each player, after selecting one of the heroes, plays a deck of 40 cards against the villain and environment decks, which "play themselves", requiring the players to put the top card of the appropriate deck into play on the villain and environment turns. On each player's turn, they may play a card from their hand, use a power printed on one of their cards in play, and draw a card from their deck. Each round starts with the villain turn, continues clockwise around the table, then concludes with the environment turn. Each villain has various advantages, such as starting with certain cards in play, as specified by the villain character card. Play continues until the heroes reduce the villain to 0 or fewer HP, or until the villain defeats the heroes, either via a win condition or by reducing all the heroes to 0 or fewer HP.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I currently played legendary and this game (as super hero cards games) and this one is way much better.

The good side of this game is that each character has his own deck of cards which plays differently according to their special powers. So you really have the feeling of playing a character.

The core rules are actually pretty simple: You play a card, use a card power and draw a card. It's the rules on the cards that makes it complex.

There is also a huge variety of heroes villains and environments which makes each game truly unique.

The first flaw I can see is that the balance of the game according to the characters, the number of players and the villain is fragile. At 2 players it's almost impossible to win unless you add extra characters or actions.

Certain villains would be too easy or too hard according to the number of players. So I think there seriously balancing issues. But since it's a coop game, the only thing it does is that the boss is too easy or impossible to defeat instead of beign the right challenge.

I played the game 3 times, the first 2 times worked well, but the 3rd was horrible. I switched to a character that was very complex, and the boss was also very simplex so it was very hard to know what was going on will all the powers active in the game.

Which leads me to the final part, there is a lot of bookkeeping which makes it fiddly and long to manage. They give you those extra tokens as reminder but sometimes you get so many ability bonuses and effects, that even with those, it's hard to keep track. That game would play perfectly as a video game, but as a board game it's just a bit more fiddly.

So in the end, it's not a bad game, but it won't please to all audiences.

RATING: 10
My favorite game, of all time, ever, no-holds-barred. I tried this at a friend's bachelor party and was immediately smitten; I probably tweeted six or seven times over the course of two thirty-minute games how much fun I was having. The game is cooperative, but challenging enough that the input of all players is needed; and the strategy of card interactions is very deep, such that not only have I never played quite the same game twice, I've had cards that I used in entirely unforeseen ways that led to improvisational victories. The game drips with theme, with bright four-color pictures and resonant superhero archetypes, while still having its own flair. The story (and there is story, though it's implied more often than it's told) is so well-written that I look forward to every expansion just for the data, let alone the card and gameplay options. If I have to detract for a moment, I *will* say that the plain-English nature of card instructions can result in some confusing and counter-intuitive situations, but they are fairly rare and for the most part have been addressed already. Also, as a bonus, the forum community for the game on the official site is very casual, welcoming, and helpful, and the creators of the game do monitor the forum and get involved in rules discussions. There's a chance that as you read this I am already playing a game, attempting to figure out how the team of Legacy, the Wraith, and Omnitron-X can take out the rampaging Plague Rat.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
This is one of my favorite cooperative games.  You play a hero who has a custom deck with three to five other players to stop a villain in an environment.  Each deck for the heroes is different and each has its own abilities. The game is really fun and even the weaker villains can be pretty challenging.  

You do need to cooperate and share information in order to be successful.  

Every villain is different as well.  I really love this game. It is very different from other games I have played. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
One of the best cooperative games ever made.  You have a pre-made deck for each hero that plays very differently from other heroes.  You are trying to defeat a villain in an environment.  The villain once defeated often continues to fight in a degraded state.  

The only downside is that low player counts have been much harder than 4 or 5 player counts and that some combinations of heroes are not complementary and make it nigh on impossible to win against some villains.  

Overall though, it is a great game and my favorite coop.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
======== Skill Floor Level: 3 out of 9
======== Approachability Grade: B

You play superheroes (original ones, not Marvel/DC) teaming up to battle a supervillain. The basic gameplay is really simple, as the complexity comes from the unique card decks of each superhero, supervillain, and environment. Any combination of these decks can be used, and the supervillain/environment decks are procedurally run rather than a player acting as the villain.

This game is the best representation I've ever seen in non-videogame-form of a traditional turn-based RPG.

RATING: 8
The best superhero game I know of. Beats all the license games 100-0 and I say this as something of a Marvel fan. The mythos of Sentinels world is pretty generic but I don't mind, it's part of the superhero comic thing. Really, I much prefer this type of oldschool artwork, over modern style of trying to be realistic and serious - guys, you are wearing spandex. Small minus for occasional fiddliness (on the plus side, setup is very easy!) and math, but other than that this is one of my all-time favorite co-op games that has simple rules but loads of tension. Replayability of the base game is decent and by buying expansion or two (preferably in publishing order as they increase in complexity) you can create so many combinations that it becomes very replayable even for the most demanding needs. Awesome storage solution too!

2-Player Comment:
*Variant forums has AWESOME 2p variant where you play 1 hero each and rest of the heroes form a sidekick deck. It seems to be balanced way to play with two and is also pretty thematic and non-intrusive.

Expansions:
+Sentinels of the Multiverse: Rook City
+Sentinels of the Multiverse: Infernal Relics 
+Sentinels of the Multiverse: Shattered Timelines

RATING: N/A
At first, I thought this was the hardest co-op ever designed (harder than Ghost Stories, which I don't like) because I misunderstood the rules and was giving the villain and environment a turn after each hero turn... That's not "each  time the heroes have all had a turn" but "after each individual hero has taken their turn".

Despite all the fiddliness, this is a really good game. As I've very little opportunity to play with other people these days, it's nice to have a solo game that actually plays as if it was designed for soloing.

Against my early thoughts I love Wraith best. Others can deal more damage, but she's so adaptable, I miss her when she's not there.

A close second is Absolute Zero, though I have a love/hate thing going on there - if you don't get out the cards that give life points for cold damage, he can be gone before you know it. Last game, I didn't draw a single one before he was down. I think he was out before the end of the third turn, which is pretty quick. He's brilliant in combo with Ra, though - all that fire damage passed on! Mister Fixer rocks! Tempest is great! Haka... meh. 

Legacy is probably my least favourite. He's so vanilla-bland, much like his inspiration, Superman. Not much of a fighter, though his Galvanize power is useful.

Supposedly, Spite is a 2 villain, but Jeez, he's impossible! Easier than the super-pants Chairman!!!?? You're having a laugh. The Ennead is super-tough, too. I can beat the others, but not those two, so far.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]02/08/2013[/u]: This is a card game that takes place in a new comic book style universe created by the designers.  Two to five heroes take on a "big bad" in any number of environments.  All participants in the battle (including the environment) take a turn to play cards from their hand giving them special powers and / or actions to play against the other participants.  Each hero and villain have a certain number of starting hit points.  The heroes must defeat the villain by knocking him down to zero HP before all heroes reach zero.

Why do I love this game?  It's NOT about deck construction!  If you take a look at my comments about Lord of the Rings LCG, you'll see that I am not competent at the whole constructing decks thing.  But here, each hero has a set deck of cards to use during battle, and every hero is different.  The variety and replayability is fantastic, even with just the base set.  Add in those expansions and the combinations of heroes, villains, and environments seems endless.

There is a lot of "bookkeeping" in this game, so keep that in mind.  The Enhanced Edition comes with nice cardboard chits to help keep track of everything that is going on...and there is a lot going on in this game.  If you're playing solo, like I do, it is a bit of a chore, but the fun of the gameplay far exceeds any upkeep.

Each hero has a different feel to their play.  Each villain acts differently than the others.  All of the environments help and hurt your heroes in numerous ways.  This is an excellent addition to our hobby and one I'm glad to have in my collection.  Fantastic stuff that I'm sure will be moving up the ranks of my favorites very quickly.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.9
This review covers all of the expansions unless I compose something separately thereupon. This is also being composed some ~10 months since last I played the game.

That is not coincidental. It is a very fun game, and also well-suited for teaching novice gamers how much fun a game can be which is more than Monopoly or Sorry. The art is a lot of fun; the creativity is refreshing; the fact of the Kickstarter success makes it delightful to support. The mechanics are easy and fast to pick up, and the game does have high replay value, especially when you really collect all of the various expansions and promo cards. But: it does, eventually, lose its lustre from playing over and again. Fun but too simple to truly last over time, for the avid gamer.

RATING: 8
Honestly, I had thought I wasn't going to like this. I mean it's co-op and really, who wants to cooperate? And the non-licensed superheros, and the simplicity.

Turns out this isn't really a co-op. It's a narrative game with a co-op element. And the theme of using fresh, new, unknown superheroes, oddly enough, makes it work!

It feels like a gang of heroes fighting off an epic threat from an insane, powerful, terrible super-villain. It's challenging, funny, intense, and manages to evoke a heroic struggle seen on the pages of the comic books. I can't wait to play it again.

RATING: 2
For a game totally devoted to its theme,
Sentinels offers precious little narrative,
one (maybe two) uninteresting decisions each round,
and brutal down-time to chew on between turns.

If you value theme over interesting decisions,
then you may enjoy Sentinels.

I can measure games by the amount of snacking I get through. The more I snack, the worse the game. When playing Sentinels, the decision on whether to eat more Doritos (cholesterol++) is more interesting than any decision I make within the game.

RATING: 2
Oh my god. Never again.

Is there a "Munchkin Supers"? Well, there is now, except here everyone gets their own pre-built Munchkin deck. Mindlessly draw cards and read tons of text, hoping you can dole out some damage to the Big Bad. Get smacked around by the Big Bad's totally random attacks. Strike back with your totally random assortment of cards.

Of course, I'm complaining about randomness, lack of strategy, etc., but BGGers have wisely identified this as a Thematic rather than Strategy Game. If I were into immersing myself in a comic-themed game with tons of cartoon art, spunky word balloons, and a whole superhero universe that riffs off the classics, then I would probably find this game very entertaining. But I tend to look for opportunities for strategy, planning, analysis, etc. You won't get any of that here.

RATING: 7.5

RATING: 5
I think this is a fun game for those that are into the superhero mythos.  Players can imagine themselves as powerful superheroes with unique abilities coming upon a big bad guy/girl and battling it out against the master and his/her minions.  

I, however, am not into superheroes.  So the game theme did not immerse me.  As a result, I can only assess this game on the merits of its design.

Game play is straight forward - play a card, play a power, draw a card. Score damage or healing as directed.  Hand size hovers around 4 cards, so choices are limited and typically there is one obvious card to play above all others.  Then you wait.  Wait until the other players complete their turns and the environment plays out then the minion goes.  Then repeat until you die or the villain dies.  A lot of waiting without a lot to think about during down time.  Again, if you are into the theme you can imagine the awesome things your team is doing with their superhero.  It's like a dungeon crawl, but with cards instead of maps, dice and minis.  I'd rather do a dungeon crawl myself.

The cards are poorly designed.  Text is small and iconography is not used and keywords are well hidden.  Tokens help draw out card effects in interesting ways, such as a big token announcing that all damage now dealt is +1, but this is only half innovative and half a cover for bad card design. 

Also, the art I am not into, though I imagine it will speak well to fans of comic books

Game plays out 20-30 minutes longer than I would like.  Some quarterbacking is involved.  I rate a 5.  I'll play if others all want to but would never myself recommend as an option.

RATING: 10
Still continues to be one of the best cooperative games I've played. The number of variations in heroes, villains and environments make for a near endless amount of replay. It also has that really great feel of being your own hero and contributing your own abilities to the team.

Yes, you really have to be into the number crunching and record keeping. Before introducing new players, I ask them if they like playing TCG's like Yu-Gi-Oh or Magic to get a feel of whether they'll like it. My way to help with this is to tell everyone to summarize their turns rather than read the text. It also helps when one person (like myself) knows all the ins and outs of every card in the game so that you can summarize what's happening to players. 

In the end, once you get into the game, it's got a great feel to it, and I'll be playing this more and more with the right people, especially with the Oblivaeon expansion coming soon.

RATING: 6.5
Very entertaining and thematic, but also a bear to manage with multiple status modifiers in play at one time as well as cards that resolve to draw more cards and other effects that cause bookkeeping to be a problem. Fun enough to be worth the 'work', but the effort keeps this from hitting the table as often as it otherwise would.

Also, game experience can vary wildly based on the combination of decks used (both natural counters and hopeless situations are a real possibility if setup is random).

Update: After further play, the book keeping really does become more tedious, but the experience is still worth it.

RATING: 10
This game, a good 2 years after purchase, is still being played weekly by my husbands group.  Yes, we have almost every expansion (OblivAeon awaiting Kickstarter fulfillment), as well as all published fanmade decks in card sleeves (links forest is hard.)  Its easy to learn/play but you have to use tactics across the table to succeed in this cooperative game.  Legacy wont know to buff you unless you ask him......I enjoy the comic book world that this us set inandhave no idea why the associated comics didnt have the demand to be printed, I'd love more story behind these!  How the Baron went frombad to good guy....how Giganta came by her powers....what happens to the great Ra?  Each deck is flavorful and unique while maintaining balance across the game.  My husbands group tries a scenario (from the online game achievements....) with their "B team".  If they fail, then they bring their "A game" and are almost unstopable.

Lots of replay value, cheap as card builders go (Pokemon?) and a very flavorful game.

I actually managed to finally get in a game of Sentinels of the Multiverse last night!
A mate invited me round to his house last night to introduce me to a couple of his gamer mates (theyâre more into wargames and role-playing than board games I think) primarily to show them 1066.  And since my new decks arrived we had two games going at once, which was great.  They had some interesting feedback, some very useful, some a bit whacky and game-changing, but they all said they enjoyed it and would play again.
One had to leave early so with three of us left we broke out Sentinels, which Iâd spied upon walking in and hoped to crack open.
Really enjoyed it!  Very interesting design, I really like how each of the hero and villain decks are unique and I especially like the environment cards that introduce new events.  There was a fair bit of book-keeping, but no more than Arkham Horror for example.  We played against Omnitron the Sentient computer, Ross was Haka the ethnic Hulk dude, Al was Ra the Sun God, and I got Legacy, who I thought was a Superman type character from the pics, but who actually turned out to be a passive support type almost Cleric/Healer character.  Since thatâs a role I donât usually play it was a little bit duller for me than it could have been I think, but actually with the buffs I was giving the other guys I was vicariously inflicting as much damage as either of them each round.  I had one Ongoing card which actually attacked but it got cancelled right quick by the baddieâs special ability.
We took a bit of a beating and the wounds were stacking up, but we stayed on top of every event and droid that came out and stacked any leftover damage onto Omnicron, eventually leading to his defeat.  Quite tense, very enjoyable.  Wish the DC game was like this!  Still not sure if Iâd pick it up though, since we have the super hero theme covered.  And as much as I admire their all new hero designs, theyâre so obviously rip offs of other mainstream heroes it just lets it down a bit.
Also discovered weâd been playing it slightly wrong after the fact, by not flipping over the villainâs ability card every turn, but using both sides at the same time, which made it more difficult!  But we werenât playing the advanced ability either (not sure if that would have had too much of an impact though: +1 damage one turn, -1 the next or something similar).

RATING: 6
I played (solo) this one while being hyped and in love with the Pathfinder ACG so my opinion on this might change a bit later.
I purchased this one looking for a good solo experience but I feel that this game really shines when played with more people.  

Pros: The superheroes' theme and the characters (there are a lot). The price is not that much as other similar games, and the components are good (*enhanced edition). 

Might like or dislike: There's a lot going on on this game for that simple rules that it has. It's all about cards and you have in a game all your hero's card (not a deck builder). The art could be improved but it fits well in the game. The replayability depends on the varied combinations of heroes vs villains and environment.

Cons: You have to keep track on HP counters, damage dealt/taken modifiers, etc... The cards modify the rules so you have to keep that in mind too (it does not have a too steep learning curve but the game demand you to "drive" it so you might not enjoy it that much on the firsts plays -especially if playing solo-).  

You can't change stats or level up your heroes while playing a campaign (what I enjoy most on Pathfinder), but that can be easily mended.

The reason that I mention Pathfinder ACG when I explain Sentinels is because I came to Sentinels [...] after some people recommended it to me for I like PACG that much.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
100+ plays. It just seems to come out regularly all year, every year.  It's a light romp co-op, another of those "let's see what happens" games (which you're either fine with, or not, so the gameâs not for everyone). Each player gets a pre-made deck, and out comes a boss villain, a baddies deck, and a pack of environment cards to fight against. On your turn, you're trying to inflict as much damage on the baddies as you can - you win if you kill the boss - and after everyone's had a shot, baddie cards get flipped and enacted, usually inflicting damage back on you. Win before you all die. There are two main issues with the game. Firstly your turn is very straight forward - pick your best card and play it, and then pick your best power and use it. Maybe you'll hold back if your best card might be even better later, so play something else instead. But most decisions are things like inflict 1 damage to everything or inflict 3 damage to one thing. Not that hard. Secondly, there's little tension in the game because there aren't risk/reward tradeoffs to be made. It's not like you're weighing up actions and cards based on the odds of whether something will happen or not - you just weigh in and play what you've got. So the gameplay itself isn't that interesting, but it plays fast and works because it's fun to get your combos out and live and die together as a team, making it a positive social experience with a great theme that I'm always happy to play. The huge number of combinations of player decks vs villains vs environments makes for a ton of different situations to overcome together, so while the gameâs simplicity means itâs not for everyone, for us itâs one of those games where the social environment it generates overcomes any mechanical downsides.

RATING: 7
What I like:
- Pure co-op with creative theme
- Asymmetric characters have distinct personalities

What I don't like:
- 2p game with 4 heroes against Spite took 130 minutes (later games were 45-60)
- Too many special abilities to track and remember
- With 2p against most villains each player must control 2 heroes

It's clearly not my style of game, but I can look at it objectively and see its merits. Definitely choose your heroes and villains as a combination, so you know what you are getting into. With a bad combination, I would rate the game a 4. With a great combination, it's a 7.

I would put the complexity around 2.8 and the depth around 2.0 for a weight of 2.4, which is a bit higher than BGG voters are saying.

RATING: 8
I've been looking for a good comic book super hero game for a long time and this one does it for me. Being a co-op is a bonus as I am a fan of those as well. 

The bosses can be extremely difficult to beat in this game, depending on what super heroes are going up against them. The part I like the most is the bosses typically have "minions" which come out each turn and must be defeated in addition to the boss, also the environment cards can play havoc on the team. 

The downside I see with this game is it could potentially be quite difficult for 1 to 3 players to win. I have only played 4 player games and have barely won.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This cooperative card game evokes the feeling of a CCG like Magic--you put out your character, buff him up with equipment and effects, and use those along with one-use cards to inflict damage on a villain and his minions (also cards, of course).  The game uses combinatorics to keep the game fresh and variable--there are many different hero, villain, and environment decks that can be used in combination for a game.  The villain and environment decks are controlled by game rules, not players.  I'd say this game is a must-play for comic-lovers who like cooperative play.  I'm neither, but still enjoyed this.

(3 plays)

RATING: N/A
Zbyszek
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
So this game has a lot going for it. The characters and villains are unique. The decks are your own so there isn't much for quarterbacking. The locations can add some interesting twists. I also like that these are "fictitious" characters so I don't have to know the background of them. It made it more enjoyable for me as I rarely know anything about comics. 

But when it all boils down to the gameplay, it feels lacking. I really don't feel like I can combo much and most of my hand played itself. You do make some decisions, but I felt like most are pretty obvious in choice. Still, even so, the cooperative nature of the game can lead to some excitement and "hold on, I'll play this" type of moments.

A lot of modifiers can get tossed around and become confusing and some of the wording on cards is less than ideal. Not to mention that a lot of the cards are incredibly wordy. Symbols would have gone a long way, but not sure how much you could really reduce down the text with how verbose and detailed a lot of the cards are.

This is one of the rare games that gets better on the app for me. I very often don't like playing board games on the phone/computer, but this simply takes care of the modifiers and tidies up the game space in a unique and fun environment. It's surprisingly well done.

Boardgame Rating - 4
App Rating - 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A vast comic book universe with an incredible wealth of backstory, Sentinels of the Multiverse has a lot to dig into.  The play mechanics are incredibly simple: play a card, use a power, draw a card.  The challenge varies wildly depending on party composition, villain and environment deck.  A lot of variables to consider.  

The only true downside to this game is the sheer amount of bookkeeping.  This is mentioned elsewhere countless times, but the amount of information you need to track and remember each round is staggering.  For this reason, I can't even play the digital app.  I need to be able to see all cards and their text at all times in order to plan my turns.  I really enjoy playing this, but it's easy to burn out with the amount of effort involved.

RATING: 7
A mixed bag for solo play. The game can feel like trying to juggle abacuses while counting backwards from negative infinity and singing 99 bottles of beer on the wall. There's so much to keep track of, so many card effects all happening at once and each with different rules or exceptions. It looks simple, but it can be a chore.

In solo play, however, it's even worse because not only is there no one else to help you remember this stuff, but you have to play more than one hero at a time. Even in multiplayer, I don't feel the game is very well balanced for the number of heroes. If I could play one hero against the villians, I'd play this more.

Own this in physical form. Multiple copies. Open, sorted, many plays.
Own this in digital form. (iOS)
Great app implementation, tons of hours spent playing the app in addition to the logged physical plays.

Not a perfect game, tracking of all in game effects can be daunting, but my god does my group love this game. It is by far & away the most played game in my collection, it hits the table consistently, pretty much weekly, often back to back & it is always met with welcome arms. The theme is perfect for us, the replayability is through the roof, & just the sheer fun factor of downing an enemy after all seemed so bleak but a few turns ago really gives that overcoming all odds comic book feel! 

Highly recommend this to anyone who likes: 

TEAMWORK in their co-op (oppose to the alpha gamer dictating everyone's turns based on the current board state.) 

COMIC BOOKS from the amazing (& constantly improving) artwork of Rebottaro, to the quotes referencing comic issues that do not exist, but inject oh so much flavor into the game, this game really is what it would be like to play out an issue of a comic. 

SUPERHEROES I have more of an attachment to the characters in this game than I do to any character that I grew up reading issues of, or watching TV shows of, or playing with their action figures, or even still now as an adult enjoying their resurgence into amazingly well done movies.

The guys who make this game are all amazingly cool & I definitely suggest you track them down at a convention (of which they attend many) & say hello. You won't be disappointed.


I can't say enough good things about this game, it would be the one game out of my (extensive) collection that I would save from a fire if I only had time to save one. Give it a try.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Definitely my favorite purchase of 2013, so far, and a title that I plan to buy any and all expansions for.

Usually I am not a fan of "take that" type deck games but this one just won me over.

Sentinels is a fast paced and challenging co-op, with a theme that is beautifully executed and completely woven into every aspect of the design. This succeeds in feeling like an epic battle between villains and heroes and not simply a puzzle that needs solving.

You can teach the game to a table of new players and have it up in running in less than 10 minutes.

The Enhanced Edition box is an absolute statement on how well thought out and lovingly crafted a game can be. You can just feel that the designers had the entire experience in mind, from set-up to break down.

The cards are a blast to look at, the game plays tense and bitter, with most coming right down to a dramatic climax. 

This is the first game I've owned that I actually feel like I have to tear myself away from in order to learn/play other things.

[b]**UPDATE** 8/14/13[/b]
After some weeks and several plays the fiddliness of this one really started to wear on me. I found the prospect of setting it up and soloing through a 3-character battle was becoming just a little bit more than I was excited to put myself through.

The theme started to fade behind the mechanics and the rinse-repeat feeling of most turns, and many games (solo & multi-player) started to feel like they were probably taking longer than they needed to for what the game is trying to do.

I remain impressed with the design, and the utter replayability offered, but sadly the overall shine to this one simply wore off through time.

[b]**UPDATE 8/26/2014**[/b]
This has now completely lost it's shine for me. I can't even make it through a solo game anymore. It's almost crazy to think just last year I felt as impressed with this as I was. I really think I might have just been blinded by how cool Expatriate was, those two hand guns just blasting away..

RATING: 2
Pros:
1. Options. There are a ton of options on what heroes you can play, villians you can fight, and locations you can fight them. You will not run out of new set ups.

Cons:
1. Fiddly. There are so many things to keep track of in this game it's out of hand. They created an app to help with the tracking, but that's almost as big of a pain to use. We spent between 10% to 20% of the time just changing the villian's track.
2. Simple. Perhaps we played with very straight forward heroes, but the cards were like punch for 2 damage, use shield to take no damage. It was boring.
3. Participation. There's always one player who's job is to just sit there and take all the damage the villian throws out. How exciting for that player right? Just sitting there getting crushed.

Summary: This game was just not exciting to me. It was a pain to set up, a pain to track everything, and didn't have a ton of excitement. I could think of no reason to want to play this game. There's nothing inherently wrong with this game. It works. I'd say it's a snoozefest, but there's never any time to nap because you're constantly updated the villian's statistics. This game feels like busy work.

RATING: 6
I must say, the first time I played Sentinels of the Multiverse I didn't care for it much. I found the art to a real turn-off and there was way too much bookkeeping involved in the way damage was dealt, even with the enhanced edition tokens.
That being said, this game gets better every time I play. There's so many interesting combinations of characters and villains that change the experience drastically. The bookkeeping also gets easier as you get more familiar with the villain and environment cards, though it still pays to have someone with good memory.
Sentinels really shines when you finally find that one villain who gives you a good beating and then returning for payback.
Overall: Sentinels can appear a bit rough around the edges. The rulebook is pretty vague and doesn't do any favors for new players. This is really a game about discovering things for yourself. If you're up for that, you're going to have a great time.

RATING: 3
my friends love this game. i really like the idea of the different villains and the environment in upheval and managing the powers of a hero! rawr! yeah! the lure is the many options and strategies a team can bring to any situation, right? yeah! okay, but the way it plays is more like co-op Carcassonne: draw and play and draw and play... little option, little choice, little sense of player agency or effect on the game. in fact, since you draw AFTER you play, the hero round sees most everyone already lined up to do the one thing they can do (very likely the same thing they did last round) without much discussion. speeds things up, i guess. my take is that the game could be more interesting without the cards, but then it'd be a roleplaying game. actually, it seems like the cards are there so that the bad stuff can cause you to discard all the time which somehow feels less punishing than a simple lost turn. if you're looking for tension, go play Pandemic. if you're looking to get beat down and punished, this is the game for you. seriously, have those hit point counters close at hand. there will be blood. anyway, i will say that it's more fun solo since then the player DOES have some options. playing 2-player with four heroes is also a step up, but juggling hands increases the fiddly factor. i'd strongly recommend you try the app before buying. oh, and get the oversized villain cards: i may not love the art, but those things are pretty cool.

RATING: 7.5
One of favorites. If you love super heroes and have been looking for a super hero game, this is it. No drafting a hodge podge of cards that don't thematically make sense. You and your friends all work together, picking heroes that you want to play, to take down the big bad. My only complaints would be that the core set can get bland after a while. I would highly recommend the expansions. My other complaint is that there is a LOT of calculation that needs to be done and kept track of and that can be off putting for some groups. I highly recommend the companion app to assist with this.

Edit: I have recently brought my review down from a 10 to a 7.5 after the honeymoon phase. Don't get me wrong, I still really enjoy this game and would highly recommend to anyone looking for a fun cooperative super hero experience. However, the time a game can take can be draining, especially with a lot of calculations even with the companion app. Pretty much what I said a few months ago, but know that it will begin to wear on you more as time goes on.

RATING: 7.5
Cooperative superhero game, full of random powers and crazy events! Developing a strategy for this game is difficult when you can't control card-draws, and the bookkeeping aspect can get a bit daunting; "Okay. I'm plus one attack from this card, but this card makes me plus two when taking damage, and this card makes my fire attacks null-in-void, but I have this irreducible attack that can't be blocked, but every time I use it everyone else is susceptible to lightning damage for one turn....(head explodes)" It really is a bear to keep track of, and you'll surely miss something.

That being said, the game is VERY fun. All the different combinations you can play with, even just in the base set, are really awesome, and the 'you-never-know-what-you're-gonna-get' aspect just makes you want to keep playing over and over again.

Well done.

RATING: 10
moderately accessible Narrative Co-op 

Love love love his one...have only played it solo, but have played upwards of 50 games of it...have shelled out far too much money for custom card designs by BGG fans, The Couldron set primary among them. Genius! Love that the chars are not held down by baggage of established superheroes, that the game has no deckbuilding, but a preprepared deck, that it ratchets up to extremely hard, and that it's so easy to put narrative on the play as it occurs.

sure, there's some adding and the like, but I don't find it onerous--and I'm often playing 5 characters & villain simultaneously!

My fave character is Titan, from The Couldron. I've designed my own version of BPRD, with him as Hellboy, and others as the rest of his team. Then I imagine ongoing soap opera style dramas based on the games played. Team members die and are replaced, villains die and are replaced, or come back from the dead. Fun!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This is a thematic cooperative game. The difficulty needs to be balanced by hand, and the game can be frustrating at times. You can adjust the difficulty by changing the number of heroes and using the advanced rules. With the new edition and the expansions, you can also balance the game by changing the value of H. 

The characters play differently, and you can try many different synergies between characters. Between the combination of heroes, the environment, and the villain, you can have an enormous number of combinations. Even with the exact same setup, you can have a very different game depending on what comes up. Occasionally the cards will just come together to either make you win or lose.

There are several poor design decisions that mar Sentinels. Many of the villains have cards of wildly varied power, but they don't play many cards, so they can basically sit there with their thumb up their butt, which isn't very interesting. This is exacerbated by heroes that can do deck manipulation, which against those villains can make them do nothing relevant. 

Some heroes are not interesting to play, and the action economy for some isn't where it needs to be for them to compete with the other heroes. The most egregious example of heroes that are not interesting to play are heroes that can make themselves invulnerable in exchange for not doing anything. Certain villains do mostly damage to the hero with the highest health, so the most useful thing you can do for the team in a situation like that is to make yourself invulnerable, walk away from the table, come back half an hour later and ask if they've won yet.

Sentinels also offers potentially an enormous amount to keep track of. In the base game that's not such a big deal, but with some of the expansion heroes and villains it can become a problem.

My experience with Sentinels has varied from excellent, engaging sessions to absolute tedium with a million things to keep track of. It's a great idea, and I think with a bit better design work it could have been one of the best cooperative games around. Unfortunately, due to those design issues I've largely lost interest in the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Sentinels of the Multiverse is a great idea for a cooperative game, and it can be incredibly fun, but it can also be monotonous and fiddly. 

My main issues with the game are:

1: The heroes aren't consistent enough in what they can do, which hurts the game thematically.

2: Some heroes are just awful compared to others. If this was part of a system in which some heroes were supposed to be stronger in order to make the game easier, that would be fine, but they're all supposed to be at the same level, and they're not even close.

3: Many of the villains have a few really powerful cards and a bunch of cards that do very little, and will either be a massive fight or complete pushovers depending on which cards they draw.

4: The game is too fiddly.

5: You don't have enough to do if you only control 1 hero.

6: Poor design choices make certain things too easy to hard counter in a completely boring way, such as controlling which cards the villain plays and making them do nothing threatening the whole game.

7: The difficulty is too random.

8: Many of the environments are annoying and feel unthematic. 

Overall the execution is poor in many places, and leads to extremely uneven experiences.

RATING: 5
Minimalistic design (play a card and use a power, then draw a card each turn, while the 'villain' and 'environment' are simply 'crisis decks') that allows for variety and creativity from cards. Could either view this as the bare essence of a cooperative game or as lacking something, and with this being a generic comic-book world with a hodge-podge of heroes banding together to fight some random villain, instead of tying to some license or established setting, I'd say it needs more trimmings design-wise to compensate for my lack of interest in the theme.

Having a separate deck for each hero limits quarterbacking slightly before players get used to each character.

3+2
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A fun co-operative "battle royale" card game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is a staple in my family. If we don't know what to play we play Sentinels. Why? It's a great cooperative game that encourages interaction. Every turn we're asking each other what we should do or asking people to do stuff for us instead of just playing our hand. We own all the major expansions and love them all. The heroes all have great flavor and each of us has a different favorite list based on play style. My only complaints are the lack of possible complexity and finikieness of the game. Each hero either does damage, prevents damage, heals damage or manages decks. So if your hero doesn't deal a lot of damage, they have to have exceptional deck control or they just feel weak (Visionary being the obvious best example of this). I'd like to see a little more than just whacking damage.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Sentinels is a 10 from me- especially once you start  adding to the base game. It's so cheap to get into, and such a fun game. There's a hero for everyone, and the ever-changing villains and environments make it so that one game is never quite like the others.

RATING: 8.5
Yes! I like it a lot. :D
What I consider the best Card game in the Superhero genre! :thumbsup:
There is so much content included in the base game, that it took quite some time for me to want to play any of the expansions. 
Even now there are some bits I haven't touched other than to organize them in the box. 
When purchased, I really did not realize just how enormous this game was.

With the fan made campaigns, Sentinels has a truly epic feel to it.
Sure some of the Heroes are simple enough that they play themselves, but there are also some amazingly complex Heroes that are a joy to decipher to maximise their capabilities.
And then we have the Villains and the locations to mix it up even more.
The variety is not just in the artwork but the mechanics and interactions between all of the decks.
I like deck-builders and constructed deck games but the static decks from Sentinels mean you can just set it up and play
The game is a bit fiddly and I was using the sidekick app to assist in my first games, but I am finding the tokens and fan created player aids provide a lot better experience (once you get used to it).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
#71 on my Top 100 Games of All Time (2015)

I wasn't impressed by Sentinels at first, but it's finally grown on me. I love that each hero has their own unique deck of cards. And those decks really feel different too in the way they impact the game. The bookkeeping in this game is atrocious, but there is an app that helps a bit. I never actually handle it myself. If I did, it might decrease in my favor. The thing I don't like about this game is that you have to constantly be referencing the many cards that come into play in front of heroes/villains/the environment to keep track of when things trigger and how they all affect each other. It's just too much for me and more than I want to do. Playing with people that don't mind keeping things straight helps except then I don't feel like I'm a full part of the team. Perhaps with more time, I'll overcome this aspect of the game to be able to engage more. I hope so because there have been many plays of this one that I really did enjoy. The sheer variability of this game given the available combinations is just amazing. Oh! And I really like playing Villains style where each hero has a villain to manage. 

Acquired: Erik

If you enjoy superheroes and want to feel like you are playing one in a real live action comic book, this is THE GAME!

+Good components
+A lot of beautiful original artwork
+Theme is flooding in this game
+A lot of hero and villain interactions
Cons:
-Some heroes are too strong and others too weak.
-Hard to track all the different damage bonuses and penalties all over the board (even with the markers)
-Game does not scale well with 2 players. Ideal number of players is 4 or 5 players.

RATING: N/A
I don't want to call this a bad game, just not one for me.

You start off really weak without any of your buffs so the beginning plays really slowly.  This is not helped by the fact that individually most cards are fairly weak.  It is then compounded by only being able to play 1 card a turn.  Then once you get setup to some degree, villains can wipe the board essentially sending you back to the start.

I wouldn't even call the game hard, just long and slow.  As mentioned you need to setup and there are definitely combos that are there to be found.  Unfortunately your choices on every turn are slim.  I often find myself with 5 cards in my hand. 2 of those can't be played because they are "limited" and already in play.  At least 1 is usually useless for the given situation or would hurt us more than help.  So often times there is only 1 actually valid option to even play.

As a side note.  This game really suffered from its art in my game group.  Maybe the style is what some people enjoy, but everyone I showed it to disliked it.  The quality seems really sub par even taking into account the style.  This made it incredibly hard for me to convince people to even want to play it.

RATING: 3
Some games are "dice fests"...but Sentinels has created a new category altogether I'll call "text-fest."  The concept of elegance is absolutely devoid in this entire game. Instead of organizing information on the cards into symbols or easily remembered mechanics, you're constantly trying to keep in mind the abilities and conditions of upwards of 10 enemy cards in front of you, not including your own or your teammate's.  If you're lucky, you'll have one guy in the group (as ours did) that was "moderating" the game and reminding everyone what each card does. 

This is sloppy, sloppy design.  I hope this unending text style is not a trend that continues. 

An absolute, utter bore.

RATING: 4.75
As a lover of games and superhero comics/films, I really wanted to like this game.  But I'm in the minority at this point, as I'm very luke warm about it.  After a few plays, it didn't make me feel like I'm a superhero fighting a supervillain.  Instead I feel I'm reading cards, and checking them frequently, playing and discarding cards, allocating damage, adjusting hit points, turning over cards, checking for modifiers of other cards and hit points, etc. - a bit tedious, frankly.  Also, wording on many of the cards seemed to us to lack clarity, and the interactions between cards, effects and actions etc seemed sometimes to not make sense (even in an admittedly 'super' universe).  Lots of things to keep track of, and lots of resorting to the rulebook, substantial rules FAQs/clarifications, and the BGG rules forum (often without success).

To me the games we had also seemed very uneven (in terms of balance), and fiddly to play - and requiring 3 or 4 players, not 2 (unless you play 2 heroes each, which makes it more fiddly and complicated and takes away from the RPG type experience).  

I do love the theme, the artwork, and the obvious passion the designers/publishers have put into it, but - to my great regret (as I bought Rook City too) - the game itself failed to grab me.    :-(

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a cooperative card game where each player plays a unique hero with a unique deck of cards and special powers against a unique villain with a unique deck of cards and powers...in a unique environment with a unique...you get the idea.

There is a lot of asynchronous stuff to experience in this game and that makes it so intriguing to me.  I love variability and even though the base game only comes with 4 villains there are also 4 different environments and 10 different heroes to play with.

Now, this is a lot of stuff but I usually roll my eyes at people that would point to something like this and say this makes it infinitely replayable because of the different combinations you can make.  For me, the combinations don't matter.  If I keep playing the same 4 villains over and over again I will get bored even if I did play in a unique location or with a unique hero each time.

That said though the actual game play was so much fun.  Each player had a unique role and unique things they could do and served a different purpose in the fight while the villain had a wide variety of nasty tricks and surprises for us.  It presented us with a very good level of challenge without feeling impossible.  I really enjoyed how it all came together.  There is also a lot of expansion and promotional content out for this game already so if you really wanted to imbue more variety into the game it is available.  All-in-all a good cooperative game.

I do have to point out that the game is probably best played with no more than 4 players.  The game doesn't do the best job balancing difficulty across player numbers.  There are some cards that scale in damage/health/etc. based on player numbers but not all and everything else is the same.  So with more players that's just more chances the heroes get to do stuff in between every villain turn with only some cards hitting harder or taking bigger hits.  I've played it once with 4 and once with 5.  With 4 the game was suitably difficult and a fun challenge.  With 5 the game was boring, we just crushed it.  I would guess the game would go the other way with only 3, making it nigh impossible.

RATING: 6.5
Co-ops tend not to excite me all that much, card games often downright bore me, and I don't have the slightest interest in superheroes.  So imagine my surprise when I discovered quite a decent little game here!  Sure, it's fiddly as all hell, but it has a lot of things going for it: many different heroes each with unique play styles, many different villains each presenting different challenges, many different settings providing unique environments, a nicely stylized superhero theme, a central mechanism reminiscent of deck-building that gives the feeling of powering up your characters, and nearly endless replayability thanks to the first few points I just listed.  It's a very good game for which I am not the target market!  Game design: 4/5  Personal enjoyment: 2.5/5  Total: 6.5/10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
This game (even the revised edition) has the most inadequate rulebook I've ever seen.  The game's owner thought that villains heal completely on flipping, which makes sense for Baron Blade but not for villains like Voss, who can repeatedly flip back and forth.  We're still not sure whether one player is always the start player, or if it rotates, or if the players can choose what order to act in each round.  The bios are nice, if at times a bit silly, but I would have sacrificed them all for the standard level of rulebook clarity.

The game also doesn't scale well; each extra player typically just means that the villain will do an extra point of damage with various attacks, which doesn't come close to matching the gain to the heroes.  The five of us actually felt bad for Baron Blade in our first game; Voss fared better but we still had loads of power to spare on his defeat.  With only three players it would have been a heck of a lot more difficult.

There are also an awful lot of cards to keep track of, which can leave you checking through a lot of text to make sure that you haven't forgotten any effects or modifiers.

But for all that, this is an excellent game!  In particular, it compares favourably with the recent Marvel and DC games.  Sentinels actually has a story progression, where what the villain is doing changes as the game goes on.  Each hero has their own deck, so you feel like you're actually playing as that hero rather than each player being bits and pieces of various heroes (as in Legendary), or having your deck composed of a smorgasbord of hero equipment and villains that you've apparently co-opted to your cause (as in DC - this is amusing, but not very thematic).  I'm not even a big fan of co-op games, but this one works for me, probably because each hero has so much stuff going on that no one can take over the group; discussion tends to be about what you can accomplish rather than what you should do, along the lines of, "I can take care of the minions on my turn if you can get rid of that shield first.  Can someone deal with that environment card before it wrecks more of our equipment?", which is the sort of planning heroes would be doing.  It's also good that there are no individual scores, since the players need to coordinate as a team and that would wreck cohesion.

Also, Tachyon rocks.

RATING: 7

RATING: 8.5
The DC Deck Building game is fast and fun.

Marvel Legendary is my favorite deck building game.  Love the heroes, the villains, and the scheme twist combinations.

Sentinels if my favorite Super Hero game though.  When I play the other games I think they are thematic to varying degrees but neither of them makes me feel like I am playing as a super hero.  Sentinels does.  What a great concept and it's executed so well with the mechanics, art, and quotes on the cards.  Each deck feels like that hero and they all play so differently.

There are so many different combinations to try out between the heroes, environments, and villains.

The enhanced edition fixed my issue with tracking health points pretty well.  

Last month I started playing versus each villain using their nemesis and two other heroes.  I will keep playing until all villains are vanquished.  I need to play this more often!

I picked up the Guise, Water Master, Celestial Tribunal and chokepoint. I think the Tribunal environment was my favorite.

This is actually a very well executed cooperative superhero game that mechanically works fantastically with it's theme. RATING: 5
This is a fantastic game that deserves it's rabid fandom and billion expansions, if you haven't tried it yet. Good for solo or co-op, it's a fight simulator where the opponent deck runs itself and you build a team and run a highly tactical session of table talk planning to work together to defeat the villain/s. RATING: 9
So gripping. Sometimes a bit fiddly and overwhelming to consider option in certain scenarios (though at other times rather straightforward). But I love the brain burn!!!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
There's so much to like here. First of all, the amount of variety is incredible. Between all of the expansions you've got an enormous amount of heroes, villains, and environments that all function completely differently. When you mix them together, you've got a unique game every time.

Second, this is the most thematic superhero game that I've played (the others being generic deckbuilders with a pasted-on theme: DC Deckbuilding and Marvel Legendary). Each hero has his own unique deck, and the art and names on the cards help give a sense what's happening. Characters put on equipment, use on-shot abilities, and use various powers to take down the villains all while dealing with environmental hazards. Being an original design is also a huge plus, because it means the game world isn't just limited to certain characters - this game can make their own versions of all sorts of popular superheros, plus other characters from pop-culture. This means that we have a game where there is an Iron Man character, a Batman character, and even a Predator villain all in the same game. Not to mention The Dude from The Big Lebowski being a playable character. Very cool.

Third, the gameplay. Unlike other game that use a generic Dominion-clone deckbuilding system, this one uses a system of unique cards that are specific to each deck, more similar to a CCG. This results in a tactical game where you're always deciding which card is best to play based on the current situation. Do I put down some equipment to prepare for the next turn, or do I use a one-shot to hit the villain while he's vulnerable?

I've only got a couple of issues with the game. First is the card quality. The cards are obviously very cheap quality but that is offset by the low cost of the game. Still, I would rather pay a little more to get better quality stuff.
Another thing is that the game can be very fiddly. You'll have several heroes, several villains and henchmen, and several different environment cards that all affect different parts of the game at the same time. This means you're constantly having to put down modifier tokens and re-read cards to make sure you're playing correctly. After a few games it gets easier, but it's still a bit of a pain.
Last, the difficulty can be really uneven because of the amount of variety. Some games it becomes obvious early on that the heros don't have a chance, and other games you just destroy everything with ease. I would really like to see some sort of official guide to adjust the difficulty based on which heroes/villains/environments are in play.

Overall, this is a great co-op that is always fun to play and the best superhero game on the market.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

#1 Got it in a trade. Really do like this game but it has its issues and they are starting to wear on me.

Without the iPad AP the bookkeeping gets crazy to the point that I am discouraged from playing. More work than I had bargained for so it loses a point of rating for that.

I will avoid the 3's and 4's for now (maybe forever).  This really decreases the pool for flavour, but the replayability should be fine because its easy to adjust the difficulty while keeping complexity low.

Good about the game: The Sentinel universe! Fun!
Not good about the game: The amount of bookkeeping just depresses me.

RATING: 8
It's pretty hard to find major fault with this game. It completely solves the quarterbacking problem that exists in nearly all other co-ops by giving each player their own unique cards. The art is perfect, the villains are great, and it's dripping with theme. My only gripes are that it is fiddly (we use the iOS companion app for bookkeeping, which helps) and that some villains do feel somewhat samey.  

Oddly enough, I think I'd like this game less if it used established comic book characters from the DC or Marvel universes. Greater Than Games has created a fantastic world that isn't restricted by the personas/abilities of existing characters.

RATING: 8
This is a great co-op game with crunchy mechanics and a lot of replay potential.

You'll enjoy this game a lot if you enjoy working against the clock, collaborating with other players to get the job done, and maximizing your own strengths.  You have to be willing to take a hit for the team, as it is possible to get eliminated personally and still have a group win.

The artwork in this game is a little cartoon-ish, but it has some hilarious flavor text on the bottom of the cards that refer back to "Issue Numbers" like old comic foot notes used to.  Great stuff!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[thing=102652][/thing] is... wow, a fantastic game! I wasn't sure what to expect since I really enjoy comics (though I don't read them anymore, because my money goes to boardgames now, but in my teens, I read almost everything since not only I bought comics, but also my friends, so we have some sort of comics club, with the comics passing hand to hand). So the theme was right in my league. I also like [thing=36218][/thing] pretty damn much. So, mechanics-wise, this one wouldn't suffer with me (I know there is players that don't like deck building). So what this game had against it? Nothing, really. I bought it twice (the first was for a friend, but I end up with the copy, which I then sold). I just wasn't sure. Now I am.

The gameplay is engaging and requires thought to make the actions of everyone work together (I only played with 3 and 4 players so far). The artwork is fantastic, setting the right mood and it is amazing that all the art is all made just for the game.

The possibilities are huge - considering the number of heroes, villains and environments that come just in the base game, and you already have hundreds of scenarios. With the expansions, this goes for the thousands. Truly no game will be the same - and even if you want the same set up, the cards will make the game different (though the feel could be the same - I can't say for sure - but in my eight plays so far, everyone feel different from the other).

Also, we fought first a villain level 1, and the battle was decided in the last cards, with the heroes seeing Death in the rear-mirror, but Ominitron fell first. The second, against a villain level 3, we were brutally defeated. I'm guessing that some villains will require a team of heroes selected just for them, but I will try to go with random heroes as much as I can - I think this is part of the fun - sure, maybe Legacy could win easier, but not always he will be avaiable (maybe he is fighting his nemesis), so Haka will have to do the job instead. -- Well, 22 plays later, I think that maybe only the villains difficult 4 might require a team made basically to face them - the level 3 villains, even though we lose a lot, I can see that they can lose to a random team with smart play.

Almost all my plays stayed inside the 1 hour (one or two, maybe, above it, by no more than 10 minutes) - a good thing, but being as fun as it is, if it took longer, I wouldn't mind, but the chances for it hit the tables would be less. One hour or a little less means more plays in my gamming group.

So, great game. I'm glad I picked this one up!

RATING: 4
but wait for 2nd ed.

We've played this game loads of times, and one of our gamer friends spent ages making suggestions for how we could have better used synergies between the characters. He would email going 'I've worked out how to make all the heroes immune to damage using Legacy's powers'. He spent four games getting the Argent Adept to work (in an expansion set). I spent two games trying to get the promo Scholar to work.

It's a LOT meatier and thematic than Legendary. Legendary is basically Ascension: The Semi-Coop Superhero edition. I love Legendary because it's simple to play, fun and cooperative. But it doesn't hold a candle to Sentinels unless your main criteria is 'accessible and easy to teach'. At no point, playing Legendary, do I feel I'm playing superheroes. As I enjoy card games, regardless of theme, this isn't a problem...

In particular, Sentinels generates hilarious stories. Like the time where four superheroes took on a gang boss in a primeval swamp. His deputy was eaten by velociraptors, and the entire underworld was then blown up in a volcanic eruption. The gang boss, bizarrely, escaped due to his flameproof underpants.

RATING: 7
I am not a big fan of co-ops, and with the high frequency at which co-ops are produced these last two years, the desire to try a new one has subsided even more. So what a surprise Sentinels was! The game just felt less mechanical or scripted than most co-ops I have played in the past, and I felt like I could really make my own choices without putting my team in danger. Gameplay wise, it felt quite a bit like a CCG with cool cards, but co-op in nature. A refreshing experience! The artwork on the cards is a mixed bag in terms of quality, but I do appreciate that all of it was done by the same artist, really conveying the feel of a 60's comic. The only drawback I can think of, is that the game does not offer any guidelines with regard to which setup is suitable for which difficulty level or numbers of players.
UPDATE: My first game with four did not go over as well as the one with two. A more complex villain made it a bit of a chore to keep track of all the card effects, especially since a lot of cards had a lot of text on them. Still like the game, but not enough to warrant a purchase.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
On paper, this game just makes a whole lot of sense. Players play individual heroes, battling a common enemy in a far-flung location. The game setting sounds just perfect for a superhero card game with individual decks representing unique powers. The variability in card play is both a boon and a big drawback for gameplay. Clearly, half the fun of playing this game is to figure out a synergy between players battling the villain. It is great when The Legacy's motivational speech can enhance damage caused by the Mist. Really cool ideas. The environment cards which I personally find annoying, can actually further increase the variability of the game.

Still, the drawbacks are somewhat significant. Like all card games, the modifiers become increasingly complicated and complex. To remember each +1, -2 modifier to stats can become a tedious exercise.  To make matters worse, there are seven to eight types of energy damage. So, not only do you have to remember a "+1", you may have to remember "+1 only to fire" or "limited +1 only to melee". All of this can bog the game down with more players as each person has to constantly remind the active player of these modifiers.

In the end, I see this game more for kids, teenagers and your adults. I see the novelty quickly wearing thin. 

Still, theme-wise nothing beats Sentinel of the Multiverse
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I've played this two times now, and I've enjoyed both plays. I just wished the game scaled better depending on the number of heroes.  I look forward to the Enhanced version. I can't wait to get a hold of that copy. Bigger box! Yay! 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
Wow is this fiddly. For the type of game it is, and the amount of maintenance that is required to run this game, just forget it. 

This would be better as an app than a real card game. It's such a clunky design and feels like something designed by a bunch of budding designers thinking about how to make a cool card game. 

Card game design has come a long way, and for someone to not at least learn from the mistakes of others just screams to me as either laziness or ignorance. I'm hoping it's the latter, but for all the hate that Magic the Gathering receives here on BGG, Sentinels of the Multiverse is far and away a poorer and more terrible design than Magic will ever be.

RATING: 7.8
Smash Up done right! This game was a lot of fun to play. Unlike Smash Up, the decks this game gives out to players are actually interesting and contain lots of neat synergy and effects, and all manage to be pretty unique.

This also takes something similar to the villain mechanic from Legendary and manages to make it interesting, fitting and cool.

I am not often impressed by theme, but Sentinels nails it. You really feel like a squad of superheroes each with their own personalities showing and interacting with one another.

Also it manages to be a cooperative game that lets each player plan enough to develop their own strategies by themselves. Unlike others where a leader will command players what to do, here you can only say "you should really try to do 2 damage to this guy!" and how you choose to approach such a command, if at all, is up to you.

RATING: N/A
A mad scientist holds the world hostage with his terrifying inventions. An alien warlord from a far away galaxy brings his limitless army of bizarre minions to conquer the planet. A giant rampaging robot cuts a swath of destruction across the coast, destroying major population centers. And who will stand in their way? A team of heroes, all with impressive powers and abilities stand between the world and the forces of evil. Will you help them? Answer the call to protect the multiverse!
\13\\13\
Sentinels of the Multiverse is a cooperative, fixed-deck card game with a comic book flavor. Each player plays as one of 10 heroes, against one of 4 villains, and the battle takes place in one of 4 different dynamic environments.
\13\\13\
Each player, after selecting one of the heroes, plays a deck of 40 cards against the villain and environment decks, which "play themselves", requiring the players to put the top card of the appropriate deck into play on the villain and environment turns. On each player's turn, they may play a card from their hand, use a power printed on one of their cards in play, and draw a card from their deck. Each round starts with the villain turn, continues clockwise around the table, then concludes with the environment turn. Each villain has various advantages, such as starting with certain cards in play, as specified by the villain character card. Play continues until the heroes reduce the villain to 0 or fewer HP, or until the villain defeats the heroes, either via a win condition or by reducing all the heroes to 0 or fewer HP.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Includes Infernal Relics, Shattered Timelines, and various mini expansions in the box.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Also have Wraith promo card and Kickstarter Playmat.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Sentinels of the Multiverse has captured the Super Hero genre better than any game that has come before. It's not perfect, as sometimes keeping all the card interactions straight is a nightmare...but generally it's worth the trouble because of the great narrative the game usually spits out.

In the broader realm of co-op games, it does have some weaknesses. The game is somewhat solvable if players build a team of heroes to directly counter a particular villain, while a random selection of heroes will often have no chance of winning. This can make for a frustrating dynamic, as finding a balance between challenge and fun can be difficult.

Despite this, there is still a lot here to love. The pre-constructed decks do a great job of giving each hero a unique and thematically appropriate feel and the environment decks do a great job of shaking up even the most predictable match-ups. There is also an almost infinite variety of combinations in the box, which only grows exponentially with each expansion.

If you love comic book stories, by all means get this game, you will love it. If you are just a fan of card games or co-ops in general, try before you buy. The nature of the game's A.I. creates some very complex timing issues and card interactions, which can sometimes get quite tedious. For me, it's worth it to slog through it when it happens, just to see how the story pans out. If you aren't invested in the plot, there probably isn't enough game here to ward off those frustrating moments.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I think this is the best 'super hero' simulation in board gaming hands down.

The super heros are varied in their abilities and the enemies are challenging and varied as well. The environments that change with each game also lend to the replayability as well as adding another element of challenge or fortune to your stance in taking down the enemey.

It is a close as I have come to portraying a super-hero working with other heros to win against a common enemy. this is not a 'tacked-on' theme.  There is no 'deckbuilding' here. It is simply a deck of cards custom designed for each hero. But knowing your cards, (or hero I should say), is important in knowing what to play and when.

"Legendary" and "DC Comics" deckbuilders, though fun to play, are not really affording you the opportunity to 'play' AS a super hero. In those games you are merely playing WITH super heroes.
 
"Sentinals" is THE super-hero card game. Period.

RATING: 3
Sometimes, just for a second, I'll accidentally have fun playing a terrible game. There's no chance that will happen in [i]Sentinels of the Multiverse[/i].

The game is positively geriatric in its pacing, as every second of play involves someone reading fourteen lines of villain, environment, or hero card text to the group.  Rarely are the card effects very interesting, either, as most revolve around statistical modifiers, card draws, or random unpreventable damage.

It's what I imagine a book club meeting would be like if no one bothered to read the assigned book ahead of time, and the attendees decided that it would be a good idea to read the full body of text out loud.  You know, for fun.

Also, I was livid when I discovered that I wasn't allowed to exit the game when my superhero was incapacitated.  After being knocked out, I was forced to twitch dully on the sidewalk and perform actions that did nothing to substantially move the game forward.  By all that is holy, JUST LET ME DIE ALREADY.

RATING: 9
I have played both multiplayer and solo.

I love this game.
 It hits all of the right notes that my superhero comics did when I was a kid.
 And, the variety is amazing. There are full, partial, and mini expansions that keep you going without feeling like someone is just trying to do "a money grab" from you, and feel like you HAVE to get them. They are optional.
 But, they actually make you wonder how they could possibly keep thinking up all of these new things, and why other companies can't do it too.

 I have played 5 and 2 player, as well as solo and love every bit. I do agree that solo can be a little confusing at first, but once you get a better feeling for the character powers, it all falls right into place.

 If you are into superheroes, you will be hard pressed to find something better!
 
Love to play. Own and Super Glad!!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I'm a fan of comic books and superheroes, especially the Marvel titles of the early 80s. I am also a huge fan of cooperative games. I now feel silly for holding off on purchasing Sentinels of the Multiverse based on the vanity that I didn't like its art (something that is definitely no longer the case). However, I took the chance based on what sounded like a very good game system with lots of built in variety in the many combinations of Heroes, Villains, and Environments.

The game has blown me away! I'm even a fan of the artwork now. The best part is how much it feels like a superhero game, it simulates the clash between a team of superheroes and an evil, megalomaniac villain in style! The very simple to teach base mechanisms are augmented by some great rules-breaking card combos, and a gameplay akin to the best CCGs out there. Each Hero is truly unique, and they have captured the essence of them wonderfully in how each one plays completely differently from one another.

You end up with widely different feeling plays based on which combination of Heroes, Villains, and Environments you select. This is a game with a ton of replay value. If you add in the expansions, you'll have enough game here to last a lifetime.

The one drawback is that the game isn't balanced in the way that you can easily deduce how to adjust the difficulty level. Yes, they now rate the difficulty level of each Hero, and Villain, but in combination with the Environment and each other, it's still hard to foresee how tough a fight you have setup.

I'm very enamored with this game, and it crept its way up to a 10 rating!

My favorite superheroes game used to be the PC game Freedom Force, but Sentinels of the Multiverse surpasses it. Although, I'd love to see a Sentinels of the Multiverse version of Freedom Force.
